  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {

        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_515a6fc6-0ceb-4924-947d-93d0dd225f88'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer11978054248385993448">Waris Dirie ran away from her oppressive life in the African desert when she was barely in her teens, illiterate and impoverished, with nothing to her name but a tattered shawl. She traveled alone across the dangerous Somali desert to Mogadishu — the first leg of a remarkable journey that would take her to London, where she worked as a house servant; then to nearly every c</span>
  <span id="freeText11978054248385993448" style="display:none">Waris Dirie ran away from her oppressive life in the African desert when she was barely in her teens, illiterate and impoverished, with nothing to her name but a tattered shawl. She traveled alone across the dangerous Somali desert to Mogadishu — the first leg of a remarkable journey that would take her to London, where she worked as a house servant; then to nearly every corner of the globe as an internationally renowned fashion model; and ultimately to New York City, where she became a human rights ambassador for the U.N. <i>Desert Flower</i> is her extraordinary story.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163017335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7103538016807846341">Wow this book left me speechless. It leaves this lump in my throat and is at the same time very inspiring. With her story Waris Dirie brings awareness to the terrible tradition of female genital mutilation in Africa. Makes me feel so blessed to be living in a country where I an live a self-determined life.</span>

  <span id="freeText734076848301612382" style="display:none">Desert Flower: The Extraordinary Journey of a Desert Nomad, Waris Dirie<br /><br />Waris Dirie escaped from her native Galkayo, Somalia, fleeing to Mogadishu to escape an arranged marriage. <br /><br />Moving with relatives to London, she worked for a while at a McDonald's and was discovered by chance by fashion photographer Terence Donovan. <br /><br />She continued via modelling in film and fashion to a stage where she was considered a supermodel. It was at this point that, with Miller, she wrote this autobiography. <br /><br />Shortly afterwards she became a UN ambassador for the abolition of FGM. <br /><br />Desert Flower: The Extraordinary Journey of a Desert Nomad is an autobiographical book written by Waris Dirie and Cathleen Miller, published in 1998 about the life of Somali model, Waris Dirie. <br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز پانزدهم ماه آگوست سال 2005 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: گل صحرا؛ نویسنده: واریس دیری؛ مترجم شهلا فیلسوغی؛ تهران، نشر چشمه؛ 1383؛ در 292ص؛ چاپ سوم و چهارم 1385؛ چاپ پنجم 1386؛ چاپ دهم 1388؛ چاپ شانزدهم 1396؛ شابک 9789643621681؛ موضوع خاطرات و سفرنامه - سده 20م<br /><br />کتاب «گل صحرا» نوشته «واریس دیری» و «کتلین میلر»، یادمانهای کودکی و نوجوانی «واریس دیری» و چگونگی ناقص سازی جنسی (ختنهٔ زنان) و فرار ایشان از آفریقا به‌ سوی لندن را شرح می‌دهد<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 29/03/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_3188749314" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3188749314" />
    <a title="W" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49365462-w"><img alt="W" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605967848p2/49365462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3188749314?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="W" class="user" itemprop="url" name="W" href="/user/show/49365462-w">W</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49365462-w?shelf=biography">biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3188749314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9346805430246662977">Waris Dirie's memoir is an extraordinary journey : from desert nomad,to domestic servant,to supermodel,to UN ambassador for the elimination of FGM.<br/><br/>She grew up in the Somali desert where life was tough. At age five,she had to endure an extreme form of FGM,which left her with lifelong damage. She was still luckier than many other girls,some of whom even died as a result of this ritual.<br/><br/>A few years later,her father wanted to marry her off,to a much older man in exchange for five camels. She ran away</span>
  <span id="freeText9346805430246662977" style="display:none">Waris Dirie's memoir is an extraordinary journey : from desert nomad,to domestic servant,to supermodel,to UN ambassador for the elimination of FGM.<br /><br />She grew up in the Somali desert where life was tough. At age five,she had to endure an extreme form of FGM,which left her with lifelong damage. She was still luckier than many other girls,some of whom even died as a result of this ritual.<br /><br />A few years later,her father wanted to marry her off,to a much older man in exchange for five camels. She ran away from home,and on the way to the city,survived a prowling lion,and attempted rape.<br /><br />Finding relatives in the city,she lived with them for a while,before another relative,the Somalian ambassador,took her to London,as a servant.<br /><br />She chose to stay on there,alone,after her relatives had left. Some moments are hard to believe. On her very first day alone in London,without any legal staus,she finds a kind stranger,willing to let her stay with her,and help her all the way. <br /><br />Similarly,when she arrives in the Somalian city from the desert,she doesn't know her relative's address or even the neighbourhood,and yet finds herself,in front of that house. Moments like these create some doubts about her credibility.<br /><br /><br />A photographer's interest,led to a modeling career,which eventually became successful. Along the way,she staged two fake marriages,to try and obtain a British passport.<br /><br />She seems to have been willing to do anything,to survive. There are some convenient coincidences,too. Help always seems to have arrived,when she needed it.<br /><br />Eventually,she started working with the UN to raise awareness,about the damage done to millions of girls,because of FGM. Today,at least,some countries have outlawed the practice.But parents of many girls continue to do it regardless.<br /><br />An interesting and unusual memoir,noteworthy for putting a cruel cultural practice,under the spotlight.She also wrote a sequel,Desert Dawn,but I didn't find it interesting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9346805430246662977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191634590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17941972951587180160">brilliant book, I could not put it down once I started reading it.<br/><br/>I read it within 24 hours, and found myself mesmerised by this womans story, and how she overcame obstacles that most of us wouldn't dream of, to get to where she is today.<br/><br/>Without going into too much detail, she managed to convey the horror and trauma of being subjected to female genital circumcision, a practise that causes more problems, than it prevents, and convinces you, that as a woman, we have a duty, irregardless of where w</span>
  <span id="freeText17941972951587180160" style="display:none">brilliant book, I could not put it down once I started reading it.<br /><br />I read it within 24 hours, and found myself mesmerised by this womans story, and how she overcame obstacles that most of us wouldn't dream of, to get to where she is today.<br /><br />Without going into too much detail, she managed to convey the horror and trauma of being subjected to female genital circumcision, a practise that causes more problems, than it prevents, and convinces you, that as a woman, we have a duty, irregardless of where we come from in the world, we should all raise our voices and try have this horrific practise stopped, before more young girls are subjected to it, and potentially die.<br /><br />The fact that it is growing, not declining is awful, and that the practise is spreading due to those faiths and nationalitys that carry this practise out are emigrating to other lands, is a revolting thought.<br /><br />I would definatly recommend this book as a great read. Get it asap and read I say.</span>

<div id="review_1789389857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789389857" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789389857?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789604101023" href="/book/show/13071129">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=biography">biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789389857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11568387251887107390">The position of women in many African regions where old customs are prevalent is very difficult. Their lives are determined by the wishes of men who wish to control every aspect of their existence, including even their sexuality. Violence, forced marriages, genital mutilation in childhood are the main expressions of this oppression.<br/><br/>A young woman tries to escape all this and after many adventures he succeeds and achieves international recognition in the modelling world, thus gaining independence </span>
  <span id="freeText11568387251887107390" style="display:none">The position of women in many African regions where old customs are prevalent is very difficult. Their lives are determined by the wishes of men who wish to control every aspect of their existence, including even their sexuality. Violence, forced marriages, genital mutilation in childhood are the main expressions of this oppression.<br /><br />A young woman tries to escape all this and after many adventures he succeeds and achieves international recognition in the modelling world, thus gaining independence and respect. But the wounds of the past, and especially the terrible experience of her genital mutilation, follow her in her new life, make her life difficult and prevent her from enjoying some things, though she is surely satisfied with what she has done.<br /><br />This eventually prompted her to tell her story and eventually write this book. With a simple language, with no unnecessary literary ornaments, which goes comfortably from humor to the most dramatic tones, she narrates in an eloqued and honest way her journey, giving a message of the courage and perseverance that must lead people to the search for a better life. At the same time, she makes a complaint of this inhumane practice, putting her own contribution in the struggle to eradicate this inhuman practice, a struggle that shows the first positive results 20 years after the writing of the book. I especially like the fact that she is doing this without rejecting her culture, for which is proud, something that is very important as many people use this struggle to pass their racist messages.<br /><br />An important book that manages to pass its message without melodramatics and exaggerations, talking about the difficulties but above all about the joy of life.<br /><br />Η θέση των γυναικών σε πολλές περιοχές της Αφρικής όπου επικρατούν πολύ παλιά έθιμα είναι πολύ δύσκολη. Η ζωή τους καθορίζεται απόλυτα από τις επιθυμίες των ανδρών οι οποίοι επιθυμούν να ελέγχουν κάθε πτυχή της ύπαρξής τους, συμπεριλαμβανομένης ακόμα και τις σεξουαλικότητας τους. Η βία, οι αναγκαστικοί γάμοι, ο ακρωτηριασμός των γεννητικών οργάνων στην παιδική ηλικία είναι οι κύριες εκφράσεις αυτής της καταπίεσης.<br /><br />Από όλα αυτά προσπαθεί να ξεφύγει μία νεαρή γυναίκα και μετά από πολλές περιπέτειες τα καταφέρνει, φτάνοντας στην διεθνή καταξίωση στο χώρο του μόντελινγκ, κερδίζοντας έτσι ανεξαρτησία και σεβασμό. Οι πληγές του παρελθόντος, όμως, και κυρίως η φρικτή εμπειρία του ακρωτηριασμού των γενετικών της οργάνων την ακολουθούν στη νέα της ζωή, τη δυσκολεύουν και την εμποδίζουν να χαρεί κάποια πράγματα, αν και σίγουρα είναι ικανοποιημένη από όσα κατάφερε.<br /><br />Αυτό την ώθησε κάποια στιγμή να πει την ιστορία της και τελικά να γράψει αυτό εδώ το βιβλίο. Με γλώσσα απλή, χωρίς περιττά λογοτεχνικά στολίδια, πού πηγαίνει άνετα από το χιούμορ στους πιο δραματικούς τόνους, αφηγείται με γλαφυρό τρόπο και ειλικρίνεια αυτή την πορεία της δίνοντας έτσι ένα μήνυμα για το θάρρος και την επιμονή που πρέπει να οδηγεί τους ανθρώπους στην αναζήτηση μιας καλύτερης ζωής. Παράλληλα κάνει μία καταγγελία αυτής της απάνθρωπης πρακτικής, βάζοντας το δικό της λιθαράκι στον αγώνα για την εξάλειψη της, ενός αγώνα που 20 χρόνια μετά τη συγγραφή του βιβλίου εμφανίζει το πρώτα θετικά αποτελέσματα. Μου αρέσει ιδιαίτερα πως το κάνει αυτό χωρίς να απορρίπτει την κουλτούρα της, γιατί οποία είναι περήφανη, κάτι πολύ σημαντικό καθώς πολλοί χρησιμοποιούν αυτόν τον αγώνα για να περάσουν τα ρατσιστικά τους μηνύματα.<br /><br />Ένα σημαντικό βιβλίο που καταφέρνει να περάσει το μήνυμα του χωρίς μελοδραματισμούς και υπερβολές, που μιλάει για τις δυσκολίες αλλά πάνω από όλα για τη χαρά της ζωής.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11568387251887107390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_282080750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282080750" />
    <a title="Ivana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6323079-ivana"><img alt="Ivana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350158310p2/6323079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282080750?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivana" href="/user/show/6323079-ivana">Ivana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9789533243474" href="/book/show/12808590-pustinjski-cvijet">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282080750" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1965555751273117548">In my opinion this is a tremendously important book. It is not just a wonderful memoir and a tale of amazing bravery of Waris Dirie, but also an detail account of FGM from the perspective of a victim. The reason why I picked up this book was mainly because I wanted to learn something more about FGM. I did learn something more, the kind of information that is personal not just theoretical. In addition, Waris does not only tell her story. She tells the story of other women she had known that have </span>
  <span id="freeText1965555751273117548" style="display:none">In my opinion this is a tremendously important book. It is not just a wonderful memoir and a tale of amazing bravery of Waris Dirie, but also an detail account of FGM from the perspective of a victim. The reason why I picked up this book was mainly because I wanted to learn something more about FGM. I did learn something more, the kind of information that is personal not just theoretical. In addition, Waris does not only tell her story. She tells the story of other women she had known that have suffered and in some cases had died because of FGM. Reading about FGM from Waris' experience( as a personal account of someone who had been subjected to it) was emotionally difficult yet I think to understand even a glimpse of what these women go to it is necessary to hear the story as they tell it. <br /><br /> What I didn't know before reading this book is that the practice of FGM is actually increasing not decreasing as immigrant are taking this terrible custom with them into the western world. To be honest, I'm sometimes frustrated by the feminist associations because to me they seem to worry about such insignificant things. Personally I don't care would someone call me signorina or signora, miss or mrs, madam or mademoiselle .There are more important problems that women worldwide are facing ! FGM is a burning issue and it deserves even more attention. There is so much violence that happens to women in the name of religion and tradition. However, in my view the practice of FGM is by far the worst thing. There are probably more victims of FGM than of wars in some areas- and the victims are mostly little girls. Unfortunately, things like this often go unnoticed. It seems to me that when people say that they don't want to interfere with somebody's religious liberties, they mean that they don't care enough to do something about the victims of specific 'religious liberties'. (What is the big thing about religion liberty anyway? Why does religious liberty often include hurting someone else? Shouldn't the goal of religion be aspiring to a personal relationship with God? Well, it's not the goal of religion- from what I see the purpose of religion is to organize people who believe in the same things so they could feel cozy and secure surrounded by people who are just afraid to question things as they are...)<br /><br />While reading „The Desert Flower" I found myself immersed in Waris' honest and simple narrative of her life. Aside for being interested in Waris' life story I also found her personality fascinating. Waris is such a brave women, a wonderful example of what is best in a human spirit. Her reflections on special moments in her life as a nomad and as a supermodel were honest and often humorous. Waris is a survivor and I admire her greatly for having the courage to talk about all the things that she so openly talks about in this book, from the FGM to fashion industry. Despite all the hardship she had endured, Waris is so full of life and ready to make the most of every situation she finds herself in. She even has courage to be a mother and to find love. After all that she has gone through, she looks at a world without hate just with concern. Waris is prepared to risk being killed by some fundamentalist because of all the things she has to tell. The least that everyone can do is listen to what she has to say- read this book and hear her out. <br /><br />I found so many of her thoughts to be not just true but also important. Many of them have gone through my head at some point in my life. For instance, why do they always make Afican models wear so much white foundation? Waris describes at one point how she felt frustrated because she felt that they were trying to turn her into a twisted black version of Cindy Crawford. As far I can see it, this is a trend that it is not going away. I will never understand why they are putting so much white powder all those female African actresses, politicians, models, TV personalities etc...When I see all those beautiful faces looking unnatural because they are painted in white, it really makes me sad. What they could be implying? It cannot be good. From my perspective, it's just racism.<br /><br />I've read this book last night and I really enjoyed reading it. I even wouldn't mind if the book was longer. (There are sequels, right? I plan to read those.) Despite the fact that Waris talks about horrific things, this is one of the most uplifting books I have read because it really is a story of survival of an amazing woman.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1965555751273117548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_679034147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/679034147" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13779-k"><img alt="K" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/679034147?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/13779-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=intense-sad-dark-or-bleak">intense-sad-dark-or-bleak</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=thank-god-i-wasn-t-born-there">thank-god-i-wasn-t-born-there</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=inspiring-story-uninspired-book">inspiring-story-uninspired-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer679034147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17107472586792086181">There is a lot to admire about Waris Dirie and her story. Raised in a nomadic Somali family, apparently raped at age four and then mutilated in a female circumcision ritual at age five, Dirie bravely ran away from home at thirteen to avoid being married off to an old man. Dirie endured a great many trials and tribulations -- finding her way to Mogadishu and to her long-lost relatives, a string of unsuccessful living arrangements, working as a maid in London and then as kitchen help in McDonalds </span>
  <span id="freeText17107472586792086181" style="display:none">There is a lot to admire about Waris Dirie and her story. Raised in a nomadic Somali family, apparently raped at age four and then mutilated in a female circumcision ritual at age five, Dirie bravely ran away from home at thirteen to avoid being married off to an old man. Dirie endured a great many trials and tribulations -- finding her way to Mogadishu and to her long-lost relatives, a string of unsuccessful living arrangements, working as a maid in London and then as kitchen help in McDonalds with minimal English language or literacy. Eventually, in an amazing rags-to-riches trajectory, Dirie embarks on a successful modeling career and then uses her success to speak out against female genital mutilation (FGM). <br /><br />It's a shocking story and it reads quickly despite the mediocre writing which detracted some. Unfortunately I just couldn't warm up to Dirie as a narrator. Some goodreaders perceived her as disingenuous, which is something that occurred to me as well although that may just be general memoir skepticism (thank you James Frey for stealing my innocence). I think the real problem was that I just didn't like Dirie. She's not someone I would ever want to meet or hang out with, although I do respect what she's been through and genuinely admire her triumph over adversity and her activism. Maybe it's cultural, or part of growing up in a tough world and having tough experiences, but Dirie seemed superficial, self-involved, and Machiavellian to me, using people when it suited her and discarding them when it didn't, falling out with family members without taking much responsibility for her own behavior, failing to respect people's wishes at times, etc. Plus I felt that some of her musings sadly lived up to negative stereotypes of models and modeling as superficial and vain. Dirie redeemed herself somewhat in my eyes with her commitment to activism, but I still felt I couldn't really connect with her.<br /><br />I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/81227.Infidel" title="Infidel by Ayaan Hirsi Ali" rel="nofollow noopener">Infidel</a>, a memoir which covered similar ground, was a far superior book with a much more relatable and admirable narrator. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17107472586792086181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1636949536" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1636949536" />
    <a title="Natasa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3742075-natasa"><img alt="Natasa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533387613p2/3742075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1636949536?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasa" href="/user/show/3742075-natasa">Natasa</a>

<div id="review_1108622994" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1108622994" />
    <a title="Mikey B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1484029-mikey-b"><img alt="Mikey B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578234137p2/1484029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1108622994?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikey B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikey B." href="/user/show/1484029-mikey-b">Mikey B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1484029-mikey-b?shelf=africa">africa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1484029-mikey-b?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1484029-mikey-b?shelf=gender-studies">gender-studies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1108622994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3751099478224555060">This is an autobiography of a very resilient and head-strong Somali woman who up and left her desert nomadic clan. She was to be betrothed, as a young teenage girl (birth dates were not recorded in her tribe), to a much older man. She was having none of that!<br/><br/>She trekked solo to Mogadishu – and from there managed through relatives, to get a posting as a maid at the Somalia London embassy. Eventually she entered the world of high fashion modeling. <br/><br/>Her Somalia narrative was intensely interesting, b</span>
  <span id="freeText3751099478224555060" style="display:none">This is an autobiography of a very resilient and head-strong Somali woman who up and left her desert nomadic clan. She was to be betrothed, as a young teenage girl (birth dates were not recorded in her tribe), to a much older man. She was having none of that!<br /><br />She trekked solo to Mogadishu – and from there managed through relatives, to get a posting as a maid at the Somalia London embassy. Eventually she entered the world of high fashion modeling. <br /><br />Her Somalia narrative was intensely interesting, but her adaptation to the West I found less so – namely her climb in the fashion industry and her “marriage” to attain citizenship. I found this book in “full flight”; the author is on the move constantly, making the book suffer from a lack of contemplation. <br /><br />Let it also be said, for those critical of her lifestyle, that if she would not have departed Somalia, she would have been tending goats, been burdened with several children, likely would have been illiterate, and dominated by a much older man.<br /><br />The author does bring up a very significant subject – at the age of five or six – she suffered the abomination of female genital mutilation (FGM). She continues to suffer from this. Apparently FGM is Africa wide. Waris Dirie has made it her life cause to prevent and educate women not to undergo this procedure. She has participated as an ambassador to the U.N. to stop this practise. It is indeed commendable for her to publicize and become a spokeperson against this.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3751099478224555060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

With grains a luxury addition to a staple of camel milk, it incidentally has a heavy 'be thankful for what you got' vibe, even before the appalling consequences of zero medical care come into view.<br/><br/>I saw the movie first; it follows the original story closely & adroitly conveys Dirie's inner voice through images.   <span id="freeText13431642829326505004" style="display:none">The best biographies take the reader to a life so alien to his own that it might as well be set on a different planet, &amp; "nomad in Somalia" comes close to Tatooine. With grains a luxury addition to a staple of camel milk, it incidentally has a heavy 'be thankful for what you got' vibe, even before the appalling consequences of zero medical care come into view.<br /><br />I saw the movie first; it follows the original story closely &amp; adroitly conveys Dirie's inner voice through images. We cannot feel the mutilation, but we can hear the screams. That bloke Nigel she lived with in England was a <i> way </i> bigger asshole than portrayed; a textbook stalker who can hold a transatlantic ticket easier than a job. <br /><br />What's wrong with it ? Too smooth ...The moments where social capital comes into play can be glaring (her first fashion photographer) to subtle (her YMCA roommate, her uncle who gets her to Britain) &amp; "luck" seems to play a role at every turn.<br /></span>

<div id="review_85748927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85748927" />
    <a title="Nnedi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1431828-nnedi"><img alt="Nnedi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507148867p2/1431828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85748927?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nnedi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nnedi" href="/user/show/1431828-nnedi">Nnedi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85748927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6786184092096145423">I love this book. Waris' time in Somalia as a child was my favorite part. It was both disturbing and lovely and wholly real. <br/><br/>What I also love about this book is the way this book addressed Genital Mutilation. Discussion about problematic tribal rites like female genital mutilation is best done from within the culture as well as from the outside. If there is no point of view from the inside all it looks like is a bunch of outsiders calling a group of people barbarians. When people feel disrespect</span>
  <span id="freeText6786184092096145423" style="display:none">I love this book. Waris' time in Somalia as a child was my favorite part. It was both disturbing and lovely and wholly real. <br /><br />What I also love about this book is the way this book addressed Genital Mutilation. Discussion about problematic tribal rites like female genital mutilation is best done from within the culture as well as from the outside. If there is no point of view from the inside all it looks like is a bunch of outsiders calling a group of people barbarians. When people feel disrespected, people don’t listen. And if people do not listen, the practice simply continues. This is one of those insider books. Waris speaks out against FGM but she also shows and proclaims that she very much loves and respects her culture.<br /><br />What I also love about Desert Flower is that it deals with FGM without having the issue consume the entire book. Waris was more than a victim of this traditional practice, much more. It's a well-rounded perspective. <br /><br />Waris' tale is simply a great one. I'm not a fan of the modeling industry in the least. But this woman's story transcends that. It shows the journey of a feisty African girl turned woman both within her traditional community and within the traditional community of the West. The modeling industry very much represents Western tradition. <br /><br />She finally goes in for the kill at the very end about FGM. All through the book I was WAITING for that, wishing for it. She summed it up really well and I was satisfied. <br /><br />My only problem with the book, wasn’t really an problem. She seemed so forgiving of the West’s issues with black women and the Beauty Myth so pervasive in the modeling industry. I think this stems from her African upbringing, where she wasn’t born and raised around racism. For this reason, her world view and the places where she directs her anger are a little different. And that is ok. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6786184092096145423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1332853140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332853140" />
    <a title="Iset" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973578-iset"><img alt="Iset" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563895104p2/4973578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332853140?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iset" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iset" href="/user/show/4973578-iset">Iset</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332853140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer680933006533243718"><br/>I picked up this book on pure chance, when it popped up as a recommendation. Since I’m interested in culture-clash and the African experience, I started reading it. Waris Dirie, who was an international model, came from the life of a desert nomad in Somalia. Fleeing in order to escape an arranged marriage to a much older man when she was just fourteen, Waris’ extraordinary flight across the desert leads first to the country’s capital of Mogadishu, and then to London, where she worked as a house </span>
  <span id="freeText680933006533243718" style="display:none"><br />I picked up this book on pure chance, when it popped up as a recommendation. Since I’m interested in culture-clash and the African experience, I started reading it. Waris Dirie, who was an international model, came from the life of a desert nomad in Somalia. Fleeing in order to escape an arranged marriage to a much older man when she was just fourteen, Waris’ extraordinary flight across the desert leads first to the country’s capital of Mogadishu, and then to London, where she worked as a house servant for several years. Deciding to make something better of herself, Waris learns British ways and joins an agency as a model, but she still has obstacles to overcome in order to find work. Eventually Waris decides to speak up about what happened to her as a child; female genital mutilation, or FGM, an event that changed her life forever.<br /><br />This book was a mixed bag for me. Dirie’s anecdotes about her life in Somalia, her struggle to understand the Western world, and her experiences with FGM varied from mildly interesting to fascinating. There were some parts I could’ve done without, however – mainly when she describes tedious and trivial everyday life bits that just aren’t essential to the overall story. In addition, I would say that the prose was fairly unremarkable and pedestrian. So I would say read for the subject matter, not the quality of writing.<br /><br /><b>6 out of 10</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="680933006533243718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3211276551" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211276551" />
    <a title="Louise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9281934-louise"><img alt="Louise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336194494p2/9281934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211276551?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise" href="/user/show/9281934-louise">Louise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=fashion">fashion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=women-s-issues">women-s-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9281934-louise?shelf=africa">africa</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211276551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18239071134069359689">Through this very intriguing autobiography you learn about the life of nomadic herders and the world of high fashion models. More striking than these desriptions is the first hand account of a female genital mutilation (FMG) and its life long consequences. <br/><br/>Dirie describes her early years of tending the family's animals and avoiding the dangerous ones. It was never ending backbreaking work. Punishments were severe. There could be days without food or water. Her mother bore 12 children, not all su</span>
  <span id="freeText18239071134069359689" style="display:none">Through this very intriguing autobiography you learn about the life of nomadic herders and the world of high fashion models. More striking than these desriptions is the first hand account of a female genital mutilation (FMG) and its life long consequences. <br /><br />Dirie describes her early years of tending the family's animals and avoiding the dangerous ones. It was never ending backbreaking work. Punishments were severe. There could be days without food or water. Her mother bore 12 children, not all survived. She had a strong bond with her mother, fun with her siblings and loved nature and the outdoors.<br /><br />At age 5, Dirie underwent FMG. She describes it, the scene, the woman who did it, her mother's compliance and support. She had great pain and was left to heal in the hut where the operation took place. There are side effects, urination takes 10 minutes; menstruation is painful and the look is horrendous. Later in life she has a subsequent surgery to correct some of this.<br /><br />At age 13, to escape a marriage to a very old man, she ran (literally - out ran her father) away. Her father would get 5 camels for this marriage, she would get a life of drudge. It took days of walking, running, hitchhiking for her to connect with relatives in cities. One relative provided a job in London. She describes her wonderment of the flight, white people, and the pace of living. She describes her life as a servant, McDonald's worker and her pursuit of her career and the legal resident status it required.<br /><br />It is quite a story. In it Dirie owns up to things she needed to do to survive. There is the dealing with a rapist, the set up marriages for legal status and how she coped with the very private matter of her FMG. <br /><br />Her story concludes with her work on behalf of eliminating FMG. You think of the millions of girls and women trapped in the situation Dirie survived (death from FMG is not uncommon - Dirie may have lost a sister from it, but no one speaks of it). <br /><br />When you see what she had to do to get away from the marriage and the unfair life she would lead, you realize how completely those without relatives in cities and the pluck and beauty of Dirie are trapped. Dirie's older sister also ran away to avoid an arranged marriage. Her simple life in a small city is most likely what (the few) escapees can aspire to.<br /><br />Interesting to this story is Dirie's mother. She grew up in Mogadishu. Her brother in law (who gave Dirie her job and ticket to London) was an ambassador. She gave up whatever benefits this family could provide for a very hard life. <br /><br />While this book is over 20 years it is timeless and deserves to be read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18239071134069359689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2535920687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535920687" />
    <a title="Diane " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/143168-diane"><img alt="Diane " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558395550p2/143168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2535920687?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane " href="/user/show/143168-diane">Diane </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=challenge-2019">challenge-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/143168-diane?shelf=ni-book-voyage">ni-book-voyage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2535920687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14215584206988417256">This was my final book of our first Novel Ideas Book Voyage. Such an excellent story, told with such honesty and bravery; bravery for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5675.Waris_Dirie' title='Waris Dirie' rel='nofollow noopener'>Waris Dirie</a> to bare her soul and open herself up to tell of the barbaric custom of FGM native to her heritage in the hope of bringing it to light and saving other young girls from the same fate.<br/><br/>While sometimes hard to read given the subject matter, this is not all that this book encompassed. It also is the story of growing up free, a nomad, in Somalia; the memorie</span>
  <span id="freeText14215584206988417256" style="display:none">This was my final book of our first Novel Ideas Book Voyage. Such an excellent story, told with such honesty and bravery; bravery for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5675.Waris_Dirie" title="Waris Dirie" rel="nofollow noopener">Waris Dirie</a> to bare her soul and open herself up to tell of the barbaric custom of FGM native to her heritage in the hope of bringing it to light and saving other young girls from the same fate.<br /><br />While sometimes hard to read given the subject matter, this is not all that this book encompassed. It also is the story of growing up free, a nomad, in Somalia; the memories she shares of being a child running free and barefoot, tending to the goats and the respect and relationships she and all of her family and all of the tribes had with the animals. No sense of running here and there, late for this and that; it's a beautiful telling. As <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5675.Waris_Dirie" title="Waris Dirie" rel="nofollow noopener">Waris Dirie</a> says "growing up in Africa she was part of pure nature, pure life. "<br /><br />I have a great deal of respect for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5675.Waris_Dirie" title="Waris Dirie" rel="nofollow noopener">Waris Dirie</a> . None of her achievements were handed to her easily, she worked (hard) with guts and determination throughout her life; and then just knows that God wants her to tell her story. I rejoiced towards the book's end when her life took on a path to what we know as normalcy. <br /><br />This book, obviously is non-fiction and I thoroughly enjoyed how it was written (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18759099.WARIS_DIRIE___CATHLEEN_MILLER" title="WARIS DIRIE - CATHLEEN MILLER" rel="nofollow noopener">WARIS DIRIE - CATHLEEN MILLER</a>) it felt as if I was sitting down and watching an interview or better yet, having a conversation with her. Very readable throughout. I would recommend.<br /><br />Thanks to my friend Melissa for bringing this woman and her story to my attention.<br /><br />NOTE TO SELF - look for Barbara Walters interview 20/20 A Healing Journey; Marie Claire article The Tragedy of Female Circumcision.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14215584206988417256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Viir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Viir" href="/user/show/63832073-viir">Viir</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127930661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5999091053334710996">I'm always excited when I read biographies, I'm always rooting and like <i>"show them what you can"</i>, <i>"oh shit, you are going to fight through this hun"</i> and be so utterly proud of their achievements and their outlook on life. The same goes for this book. Waris Dirie is an admirable woman. She went through shit, and yeah her personality would clash with a lot of people (I probably couldn't handle her, I like quite people like myself) but she worked for everything she got and had her portion of luck s</span>
  <span id="freeText5999091053334710996" style="display:none">I'm always excited when I read biographies, I'm always rooting and like <i>"show them what you can"</i>, <i>"oh shit, you are going to fight through this hun"</i> and be so utterly proud of their achievements and their outlook on life. The same goes for this book. Waris Dirie is an admirable woman. She went through shit, and yeah her personality would clash with a lot of people (I probably couldn't handle her, I like quite people like myself) but she worked for everything she got and had her portion of luck she deserved. A girl from Somalia, fleeing by herself, conquering the world not only because of her looks but also because of her will and her unique character.<br /><br />In my copy of the book you can find two articles at the end of the actual book and let me tell you: <b>it was more sad than the actual story</b>. I was so happy for her, for finding love and success and having this voice against female genital mutilation. And the articles just opened this hole of misery and showed another side of her, the after effects of her life basically, that I hoped and till then believed she didn't have. I don't know what she is doing now but I hope life has been good to her and her family.<br /><br />The only reason why I take one star off is because of the narrative. She goes back and forth in time without actually explaining where we are now. She would talk about her life in London and suddenly we are back again in Mogadishu and learning more about it. Sometimes it was really irritating but on the other hand, it also makes sense: <b>time means nothing for Waris Dirie</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5999091053334710996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928560159?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lorraine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lorraine" href="/user/show/12034546-lorraine">Lorraine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781860497582" href="/book/show/8747.Desert_Flower">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12034546-lorraine?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928560159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9944176512199172704">Waris had an extraordinary story to tell but the narration left much to be desired. I suppose writing an autobiography is so subjective. Opens one up to scrutiny. What to put in. What to leave out. The story left a bitter taste in my mouth.<br/><br/>From page 15 to page 224, the narration is flat, flat, flat. As much as her events are chronologically laid out, there was no hook for me as the reader. I kept thinking "where's the rising action?". The one event that would lead to the peak of her story. Nothi</span>
  <span id="freeText9944176512199172704" style="display:none">Waris had an extraordinary story to tell but the narration left much to be desired. I suppose writing an autobiography is so subjective. Opens one up to scrutiny. What to put in. What to leave out. The story left a bitter taste in my mouth.<br /><br />From page 15 to page 224, the narration is flat, flat, flat. As much as her events are chronologically laid out, there was no hook for me as the reader. I kept thinking "where's the rising action?". The one event that would lead to the peak of her story. Nothing. Even her meeting her mother after a 15 year hiatus plateau ed.<br /><br />From page 224, she becomes a UN ambassador fighting against female genital mutilation. Now that is when her story became interesting to me. I am not for one minute advocating that books with a social element pique my interest, but I feel that she should have chosen a common theme and expanded on it.<br /><br />The diction. Now that was a thorn on my backside. It felt wrong. Pretentious. Borrowed. Let's blame it on the language barrier. Or rather, let's not. I'd like to believe that when you decide to write, especially an autobiography and your name is Waris, you get assigned a whole literary team. Her's felt like a "basement bargain" team. Firstly, for an African from a sheltered Somali nomadic culture, her constant use of profanity was quite astonishing. Bordered on the bizarre. Her insincere nature was also quite puzzling. Marrying the Irish getriatic I was like "WTF", so out of character. Then she repeats it by marrying Nigel. I take it that she was under pressure and the threat of deportation hung like a jaggered sword over her head but, there were other less dangerous avenues to be explored. Applying for asylum. Her country was in turmoil civilly after all.<br /><br />Is she still married to Nigel the nut? Is she still with Dana? Did she ever build a house for her family!<br /><br />AND, Elton John bought the rights to the movie??? Nuff said</span>
  <a data-text-id="9944176512199172704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3040126302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3040126302" />
    <a title="Charles Edwards-Freshwater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75779839-charles-edwards-freshwater"><img alt="Charles Edwards-Freshwater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575812240p2/75779839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3040126302?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charles Edwards-Freshwater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charles Edwards-Freshwater" href="/user/show/75779839-charles-edwards-freshwater">Charles Edwards-Freshwater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75779839-charles-edwards-freshwater?shelf=30-before-30">30-before-30</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3040126302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9066216473591827793">I don't often read non-fiction and I usually avoid memoirs and biographies as there are few people that I'm intrigued enough about to make reading about their whole lives worthwhile. However, as this book was suggested to me as one of my 30 before 30 options, I decided to pick it up anyway. Powerful. compelling and filled with astute observation, outrage and gratitude, Desert Flower has changed my mind about memoirs, especially as Waris has lead such a rich and exciting life.<br/><br/>I think what struck </span>
  <span id="freeText9066216473591827793" style="display:none">I don't often read non-fiction and I usually avoid memoirs and biographies as there are few people that I'm intrigued enough about to make reading about their whole lives worthwhile. However, as this book was suggested to me as one of my 30 before 30 options, I decided to pick it up anyway. Powerful. compelling and filled with astute observation, outrage and gratitude, Desert Flower has changed my mind about memoirs, especially as Waris has lead such a rich and exciting life.<br /><br />I think what struck me most about this book is how much it taught me about Somalian culture and the lifestyle they lead - I was completely ignorant of how people lived in the country before reading this, and Waris instantly painted the picture of her culture and childhood in such a fascinating and beautiful way. Yes life is hard, there are droughts, there is death and suffering, but there is also so much beauty - nature is a key part of life for these people, rain is a blessing, even rice is something to be savoured. It's a beautiful balance and something that Westerners can never truly understand, and that Waris successfully gives us a glimpse of as something sacred and wonderful.<br /><br />In many ways Waris is incredibly lucky - she's a fighter, a brave soul who takes no crap and a feminist icon, but she has a good heart and understands the need for compassion and kindness alongside the need to stick up for herself and her own values. It was amazing to read about all of the plight she had been through and how she took all of these risks and exciting leaps of faith to become one of the most regarded models of her time. There was a lot of luck involved too - imagine being scouted from the streets these days? But I think her life is one of those rare occasions where the stars align for good reason.<br /><br />The most moving parts of this book are undoubtedly about FGM. I knew about the practice, but I had no clue that it was still as widespread as millions of unfortunate women undergoing this treatment even today. Waris helped bring such awareness to this issue, and her views of male oppression and the dangers of culture and ingrained acts such as this and what it means for the status and health of women is something that everyone should educate themselves about.<br /><br />If I did have to find any problems with this book i would say that after Waris gets deeply entrenched into the fashion industry I did lose a bit of interest. I think I'm not invested enough in the fashion industry, but it was nice to get a snapshot of what life behind the scenes for a top model constituted back in the day.<br /><br />Overall, it's a stunning book and a tale of bravery that is really very unique. I highly recommend it.<br /><br />4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9066216473591827793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176814081?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LG" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LG" href="/user/show/5263231-lg">LG</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of biographies</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176814081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer85311519089933569"><i>Anne Russell wrote: “This is an easy read that gives one insight into female circumcision. One finishes the book with an interest to learn more about the issue and how effective the work the UN has done. It also provides an angle on the illegal immigrant story that is not as grim as so many tales are. For those of us living overseas one can appreciate her reflections in the end about being a nomad yet being very loyal to Somalia despite its problems.”</i><br/><br/>I read this memoir a couple of years back. I </span>
  <span id="freeText85311519089933569" style="display:none"><i>Anne Russell wrote: “This is an easy read that gives one insight into female circumcision. One finishes the book with an interest to learn more about the issue and how effective the work the UN has done. It also provides an angle on the illegal immigrant story that is not as grim as so many tales are. For those of us living overseas one can appreciate her reflections in the end about being a nomad yet being very loyal to Somalia despite its problems.”</i><br /><br />I read this memoir a couple of years back. I agree: Dirie, a supermodel and former Bond girl, writes about her pre-catwalk life in a straightforward and engaging way. Sad to admit, I had (OK, still have) a bit of prejudice against models, given the self-involved image they project in their media. (OK, there’s a bit of sour grapes in there too.) But Dirie used her high profile to speak out against female genital mutilation (FGM) and, admirably, quit modeling to establish the anti-FGM <a href="&lt;br /&gt;http://www.desertflowerfoundation.org/en/" rel="nofollow noopener">Desert Flower Foundation</a> and other humanitarian organizations. Her literal and figurative journey from hardship and hard work to success and activism is inspiring. The <a href="http://www.desertflower-movie.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">2009 movie</a> based on this book has apparently been released in several countries – would that I could get my hands on it.<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer10101273605430942267">I feel like I must do my part for the Goodreads community and tell you all that this is truly a terrible book. <br/><br/>The characters and their actions make no sense. Gratuitous profanity! The overuse of onomatopoeias such as "beep beep!", "phew!", and "shhhhh"! (That last sound is the sound of, as Waris would put it, "pee-pee and poo-poo".) And Waris herself, who I want to understand and admire, but who I cannot help but dislike because her internal monologue never goes much farther than the two basic </span>
  <span id="freeText10101273605430942267" style="display:none">I feel like I must do my part for the Goodreads community and tell you all that this is truly a terrible book. <br /><br />The characters and their actions make no sense. Gratuitous profanity! The overuse of onomatopoeias such as "beep beep!", "phew!", and "shhhhh"! (That last sound is the sound of, as Waris would put it, "pee-pee and poo-poo".) And Waris herself, who I want to understand and admire, but who I cannot help but dislike because her internal monologue never goes much farther than the two basic lines of "I have always known that I was special" and "Motherf*cker! I hate this person! Who do they think they are?". <br /><br />I don't know what's worse. Waris Dirie painting herself in such an immature, repugnant light in her own work, or a shabby editor/ghost writer letting their client tarnish themselves in print?<br /><br /> It does not matter if this review gets submerged by the many other ones, it does not matter if only one person gets to read it. What matters is that the disappointing mediocrity of this novel must be exposed at all costs in order to avoid other students, like me, from reading this roll of toilet paper as a part of their English curriculum.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9709259030493760238">I just... I don't even know how to begin to say how inspired I was by Waris' story. It was harrowing in many places and yet somehow, against all odds, she has not only survived but emerged resilient. She shows such bravery in fighting back against the scourge of Female Genital Mutilation. It is such a hugely personal and difficult thing to discuss but she has done it, not fearlessly but despite her fear and doing so helped to bring this important issue back into the public's attention. Horrifica</span>
  <span id="freeText9709259030493760238" style="display:none">I just... I don't even know how to begin to say how inspired I was by Waris' story. It was harrowing in many places and yet somehow, against all odds, she has not only survived but emerged resilient. She shows such bravery in fighting back against the scourge of Female Genital Mutilation. It is such a hugely personal and difficult thing to discuss but she has done it, not fearlessly but despite her fear and doing so helped to bring this important issue back into the public's attention. Horrifically, it is something that still takes place today - my sister, for example, who is a school teacher (in the UK) underwent training only a year or so ago on how to recognise signs of FGM in her pupils. On the plus side, of course, this does mean people are standing up and taking notice. And Waris is still fighting. I was crying as I finished reading this - what a truly amazing woman.</span>

<div id="review_43065497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43065497" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69671-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43065497?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/69671-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69671-kelly?shelf=autobiography-biography">autobiography-biography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43065497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11308859045369949295">Waris Dirie is a former supermodel (famous in the 1980's and 1990's) who grew up as a nomad in Somalia. Around age 12 or 13, she ran away from home to avoid an arranged marriage to a much older man, and she eventually made her way to London, where she was "discovered" after several years. Soon thereafter, she ended up in a James Bond movie (the terrible one with Timothy Dalton) and appeared in calendars, major magazines, and Revlon ads worldwide.<br/><br/>What is truly impressive about this spunky and cou</span>
  <span id="freeText11308859045369949295" style="display:none">Waris Dirie is a former supermodel (famous in the 1980's and 1990's) who grew up as a nomad in Somalia. Around age 12 or 13, she ran away from home to avoid an arranged marriage to a much older man, and she eventually made her way to London, where she was "discovered" after several years. Soon thereafter, she ended up in a James Bond movie (the terrible one with Timothy Dalton) and appeared in calendars, major magazines, and Revlon ads worldwide.<br /><br />What is truly impressive about this spunky and courageous woman, however, is her frank discussion of her infibulation as a young girl (the most severe form of female genital mutilation). After rising to the height of fame as a model, Waris decided to go public in Marie Claire with her identity as an infibulated woman, after she had suffered in silence for years with the shame and physical complications of her "circumcision." Because of her courageous interview in Marie Claire, Waris ended up on 20/20, and the UN eventually named her its special ambassador on FGM.<br /><br />Waris grew up an uneducated nomad, but I was struck by the honesty and simplicity of her prose, and I realized that she has an incredible natural talent for storytelling. I became so engrossed in her autobiography on the train one day that I almost missed my stop! Luckily, my stop was the last one, so the conductor had to tell me to stop reading and get off the train. I had completely gotten sucked into her story. I highly recommend this book, as long as one can stomach the very graphic description of Waris' infibulation. That part, and her subsequent discussions of the complications that arose from the operation, brought me to tears. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11308859045369949295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_152967107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152967107" />
    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1730194-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230665575p2/1730194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152967107?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/1730194-alicia">Alicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152967107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736014638250744638">Wow! This is the true story of Waris Dirie. Born as a nomad in Somailia, at age 13 she ran away from home to avoid an arranged marriage to a much older man, and she eventually made her way to London, where she was "discovered" after several years and became an international supermodel and even appeared in a James Bond movie.<br/><br/>Her story is unbelievable! I especially loved reading about her life growing up as a nomad - their only nutrition was camel's milk, they slept outside, worked hard (she had h</span>
  <span id="freeText1736014638250744638" style="display:none">Wow! This is the true story of Waris Dirie. Born as a nomad in Somailia, at age 13 she ran away from home to avoid an arranged marriage to a much older man, and she eventually made her way to London, where she was "discovered" after several years and became an international supermodel and even appeared in a James Bond movie.<br /><br />Her story is unbelievable! I especially loved reading about her life growing up as a nomad - their only nutrition was camel's milk, they slept outside, worked hard (she had her own herd of goats at the age of 5), and survival was always uncertain. <br /><br />What is truly impressive about this spunky and courageous woman, however, is her frank discussion of her infibulation as a young girl (the most severe form of female genital mutilation). After rising to the height of fame as a model, Waris decided to go public in Marie Claire with her identity as an infibulated woman, after she had suffered in silence for years with the shame and physical complications of her "circumcision." Because of her courageous interview in Marie Claire, Waris ended up on 20/20, and the UN eventually named her its special ambassador on FGM. <br /><br />There was some swearing and it was a little disappointing for me that she didn't do more with her money. She said her goal was simply to earn enough money to buy her mother a home but it seemed like she always spent every penny she earned and never gave anything to others. Other than that it was superb!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1736014638250744638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('otL97i+FL0aezpByGkGKx/HjT5x0cRvlp49WuDG5k7GYk+GwEJ1fzobiEfQYu1JUwcY7MZTt5s5unjKtximZIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
